      <p><b>Paraguay</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Spanish pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[paɾaˈɣwaj]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:ES-pe_-_Paraguay.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/ES-pe_-_Paraguay.ogg" class="internal" title="ES-pe - Paraguay.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), officially the <b>Republic of Paraguay</b> (Spanish: <i lang="es">República del Paraguay</i>; Guarani: <i lang="gn">Tetã Paraguái</i>), is a country in South America. It is bordered by Argentina to the south and southwest, Brazil to the east and northeast, and Bolivia to the northwest. Although one of only two landlocked countries in South America (the other being Bolivia), the country has coasts,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> beaches<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> and ports on the <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">Paraná</a> rivers that give exit to the Atlantic Ocean through the Paraná-Paraguay Waterway.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadores</a> arrived in 1524, and in 1537 established the city of <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunción">Asunción</a>, the first capital of the <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Governorate of the Río de la Plata">Governorate of the Río de la Plata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> During the 17th century, Paraguay was the center of <a href="/wiki/Reductions" title="Reductions">Jesuit missions</a>, where the native <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guaraní people</a> were converted to Christianity and introduced to European culture.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Suppression_of_the_Society_of_Jesus" title="Suppression of the Society of Jesus">expulsion of the Jesuits</a> from Spanish territories in 1767, Paraguay increasingly became a peripheral colony, with few urban centers and settlers. Following <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Paraguay" title="Independence of Paraguay">independence from Spain</a> in the early 19th century, Paraguay was ruled by a series of authoritarian governments characterized by nationalist, isolationist and <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionist</a> policies. This period ended with the disastrous <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a> (1864–70), during which the country lost half its prewar population and around 25–33% of its territory to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Triple_Alliance" title="Treaty of the Triple Alliance">Triple Alliance</a> of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>. In the 20th century, Paraguay faced another major international conflict—the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a> (1932–35) against Bolivia—in which it prevailed. Afterwards, the country came under a succession of military dictators, culminating in the 35-year regime of <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Stroessner" title="Alfredo Stroessner">Alfredo Stroessner</a>, which lasted until his overthrow in 1989 by an internal military coup. This marked the beginning of Paraguay's democratic era, which continues to this day. </p>
      <p>Paraguay is a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> It is a founding member of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lima_Group" title="Lima Group">Lima Group</a>. Additionally, the city of <a href="/wiki/Luque" title="Luque">Luque</a>, in metropolitan Asuncion, is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">South American Football Confederation</a>. </p>
      <p>The majority of Paraguay's seven million people are <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a></i>, and Guarani culture remains widely influential; more than 90% of the population speak various dialects of the <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani language</a> alongside Spanish. Despite a history of poverty and political repression, Paraguay often ranks as the "world's happiest place" based on global polling data.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>From <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani</a> <i>paraguá</i> "feather crown", thus <i>paraguaí</i> "river of crowns".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Paraguay" title="History of Paraguay">History of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_era">Pre-Columbian era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous people">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guaraní</a> had been living in eastern Paraguay for at least a millennium before the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a>. Western Paraguay, the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a>, was inhabited by nomads of whom the <a href="/wiki/Guaycuru" class="mw-redirect" title="Guaycuru">Guaycuru</a> peoples were the most prominent. The Paraguay River was roughly the dividing line between the agricultural Guarani people to the east and the nomadic and semi-nomadic people to the west in the Gran Chaco. The Guarcuru nomads were known for their warrior traditions and were not fully pacified until the late 19th century. These indigenous tribes belonged to five distinct language families, which were the bases of their major divisions. Differing language speaking groups were generally competitive over resources and territories. They were further divided into tribes by speaking languages in branches of these families. Today 17 separate <a href="/wiki/Ethnolinguistics" title="Ethnolinguistics">ethnolinguistic</a> groups remain. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonization">Colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The first Europeans in the area were Spanish explorers in 1516.<sup id="cite_ref-eec_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eec-20">[18]</a></sup> The Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Salazar_de_Espinosa" title="Juan de Salazar de Espinosa">Juan de Salazar de Espinosa</a> founded the settlement of <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunción">Asunción</a> on 15 August 1537. The city eventually became the center of a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonial province of Paraguay</a>. </p>
      <p>An attempt to create an autonomous Christian Indian nation<sup id="cite_ref-cite_wdl|#2581_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cite_wdl|#2581-21">[19]</a></sup> was undertaken by <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> missions and settlements in this part of South America in the eighteenth century. They developed <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_reduction" title="Jesuit reduction">Jesuit reductions</a> to bring Guarani populations together at Spanish missions and protect them from virtual slavery by Spanish settlers and Portuguese slave raiders, the <a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">Bandeirantes</a>, in addition to seeking their conversion to Christianity. Catholicism in Paraguay was influenced by the indigenous peoples; the <a href="/wiki/Syncretic" class="mw-redirect" title="Syncretic">syncretic</a> religion has absorbed native elements. The <i>reducciones</i> flourished in eastern Paraguay for about 150 years, until the expulsion of the Jesuits by the Spanish Crown in 1767. The ruins of two 18th-century <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_Missions_of_La_Sant%C3%ADsima_Trinidad_de_Paran%C3%A1_and_Jes%C3%BAs_de_Tavarangue" title="Jesuit Missions of La Santísima Trinidad de Paraná and Jesús de Tavarangue">Jesuit Missions of La Santísima Trinidad de Paraná and Jesús de Tavarangue</a> have been designated as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cite_wdl|#2581_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cite_wdl|#2581-21">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In western Paraguay, Spanish settlement and Christianity were strongly resisted by the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Guaycuru_peoples" title="Guaycuru peoples">Guaycuru</a> and other nomads from the 16th century onward. Most of these peoples were absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> population in the 18th and 19th centuries. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_rule_of_Francia">Independence and rule of Francia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Independence and rule of Francia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Paraguay" title="Independence of Paraguay">Independence of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg/170px-Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg/255px-Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg/340px-Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1434" data-file-height="1681"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia" title="José Gaspar Rodríguez de Francia">José Gaspar Rodríguez de Francia</a>, Paraguay's first dictator.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay overthrew the local Spanish administration on 14 May 1811. Paraguay's first dictator was <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia" title="José Gaspar Rodríguez de Francia">José Gaspar Rodríguez de Francia</a> who ruled Paraguay from 1814 until his death in 1840, with very little outside contact or influence. He intended to create a <a href="/wiki/Utopian" class="mw-redirect" title="Utopian">utopian</a> society based on the French theorist <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Social_Contract" title="The Social Contract"><i>Social Contract</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> Rodríguez de Francia was nicknamed <i>El Supremo</i>. </p>
      <p>Rodríguez de Francia established new laws that greatly reduced the powers of the Catholic church (Catholicism was then an established state religion) and the cabinet, forbade colonial citizens from marrying one another and allowed them to marry only blacks, <a href="/wiki/Mulattoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Mulattoes">mulattoes</a> or natives, in order to break the power of colonial-era elites and to create a <a href="/wiki/Mixed-race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> or mestizo society.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> He cut off relations between Paraguay and the rest of South America. Because of Francia's restrictions of freedom, <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Yegros" title="Fulgencio Yegros">Fulgencio Yegros</a> and several other Independence-era leaders in 1820 planned a <i>coup d’état</i> against Francia, who discovered the plot and had its leaders either executed or imprisoned for life.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Rule_of_the_L.C3.B3pez_family"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_of_the_López_family">Rule of the López family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rule of the López family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil,_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg/280px-1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg/420px-1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg/560px-1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3203"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil,_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Political map of the region, 1864
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After Francia's death in 1840, Paraguay was ruled by various military officers under a new <i><a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">junta</a></i>, until <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Antonio_L%C3%B3pez" title="Carlos Antonio López">Carlos Antonio López</a> (allegedly Rodríguez de Francia's nephew) came to power in 1841. López modernized Paraguay and opened it to foreign commerce. He signed a <a href="/wiki/Non-aggression_pact" title="Non-aggression pact">non-aggression pact</a> with Argentina and officially declared independence of Paraguay in 1842. After López's death in 1862, power was transferred to his eldest son, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Solano_L%C3%B3pez" title="Francisco Solano López">Francisco Solano López</a>. </p>
      <p>The regime of the López family was characterized by pervasive and rigid centralism in production and distribution. There was no distinction between the public and the private spheres, and the López family ruled the country as it would a large estate.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government exerted control on all exports. The export of <a href="/wiki/Yerba_mate" title="Yerba mate">yerba mate</a> and valuable wood products maintained the balance of trade between Paraguay and the outside world.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> The Paraguayan government was extremely protectionist, never accepted loans from abroad and levied high <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> against imported foreign products. This <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionism</a> made the society self-sufficient, and it also avoided the debt suffered by Argentina and Brazil. Slavery existed in Paraguay, although not in great numbers, until 1844, when it was legally abolished in the new constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193339-40_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193339-40-27">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Solano_L%C3%B3pez" title="Francisco Solano López">Francisco Solano López</a>, the son of Carlos Antonio López, replaced his father as the President-Dictator in 1862, and generally continued the political policies of his father. Both wanted to give an international image of Paraguay as "democratic and republican", but in fact, the ruling family had almost total control of all public life in the country, including church and colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193341-42_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193341-42-28">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Militarily, Carlos Antonio López modernized and expanded industry and the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_Army" title="Paraguayan Army">Paraguayan Army</a> and greatly strengthened the strategic defenses of Paraguay by developing the <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Humait%C3%A1" title="Fortress of Humaitá">Fortress of Humaitá</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> The government hired more than 200 foreign technicians, who installed <a href="/wiki/Telegraph_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Telegraph line">telegraph lines</a> and railroads to aid the expanding steel, textile, paper and ink, naval construction, weapons and gunpowder industries. The <a href="/wiki/Ybycu%C3%AD" title="Ybycuí">Ybycuí</a> foundry, completed in 1850, manufactured cannons, mortars and bullets of all calibers. River warships were built in the shipyards of Asunción. Fortifications were built, especially along the <a href="/wiki/Apa_River" title="Apa River">Apa River</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hooker_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hooker-30">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>22</span></sup> The work was continued by his son Francisco Solano and in terms of socio-economic development, the country was dubbed as "the most advanced Republic in South America", notably by the British judge and politician <a href="/wiki/Robert_Phillimore" title="Robert Phillimore">Sir Robert Phillimore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to George Thompson, Lieutenant Colonel of Engineers in the Paraguayan Army prior to and during the war, López's government was comparatively a good one for Paraguay: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>Probably in no other country in the world has life and property been so secure as all over Paraguay during his (Antonio Lopez's) reign. Crime was almost unknown, and when committed, immediately detected and punished. The mass of the people was, perhaps, the happiest in existence. They had hardly to do any work to gain a livelihood. Each family had its house or hut in its own ground. They planted, in a few days, enough tobacco, maize and mandioca for their own consumption [...]. Having at every hut a grove of oranges [...] and also a few cows, they were almost throughout the year under little necessity [...]. The higher classes, of course, lived more in the European way...</p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        — <cite>George Thompson, C.E.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson186910_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson186910-32">[30]</a></sup></cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote> 
      <h3><span id="Paraguayan_War_.281864.E2.80.931870.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Paraguayan_War_(1864–1870)">Paraguayan War (1864–1870)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Paraguayan War (1864–1870)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War_casualties" title="Paraguayan War casualties">Paraguayan War casualties</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_(From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg/170px-FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg/255px-FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg/340px-FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="872" data-file-height="1028"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_(From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Solano_L%C3%B3pez" title="Francisco Solano López">Francisco Solano López</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 12 October 1864, despite Paraguayan ultimatums, <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Brazil</a> (sided with the Argentine Government under General <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Mitre" title="Bartolomé Mitre">Bartolomé Mitre</a> and the rebellious <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Party_(Uruguay)" title="Colorado Party (Uruguay)">Uruguayan colorados</a> led by Gen. <a href="/wiki/Venancio_Flores" title="Venancio Flores">Venancio Flores</a>) invaded the Republic of Uruguay in order to overthrow the government of that time (which was under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(Uruguay)" title="National Party (Uruguay)">Blanco Party</a>, an ally of López),<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> thus starting the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Paraguayans, led by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_marshal" title="Grand marshal">Marshal of the Republic</a> Francisco Solano López, retaliated by <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso_Campaign" title="Mato Grosso Campaign">attacking the Matto Grosso</a> on 15 December 1864 and later declared war against Argentina on 23 March 1865. The "Blanco Government" was toppled and replaced by a "Colorado Government" under General Venancio Flores on 22 February 1865 and afterwards, the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Argentine Republic">Argentine Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> and the Republic of Uruguay signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Triple_Alliance" title="Treaty of the Triple Alliance">Secret Treaty of the Triple Alliance</a> against the Paraguayan Government, on 1 May 1865.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Paraguayans held a ferocious resistance but were ultimately defeated in 1870 in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cerro_Cor%C3%A1" title="Battle of Cerro Corá">Battle of Cerro Corá</a>, where Marshal Solano López was killed in action, refusing to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> The real causes of this war, which remains the bloodiest international conflict in the history of <a href="/wiki/The_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Americas">The Americas</a>, are still highly debated.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TuyutiDetail.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuyutiDetail.jpg/220px-TuyutiDetail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuyutiDetail.jpg/330px-TuyutiDetail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuyutiDetail.jpg/440px-TuyutiDetail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1446" data-file-height="945"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TuyutiDetail.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tuyut%C3%AD" title="Battle of Tuyutí">Battle of Tuyutí</a>, May 1866
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay lost 25–33% of its territory to Argentina and Brazil, was forced to pay an enormous war debt and to sell large amounts of national properties in order to restore its internal budget. But the worst consequence of the war was the catastrophic loss of population. At least 50% of the Paraguayans died during the conflict, numbers which took many decades for the country to return to. About the disaster suffered by the Paraguayans at the outcome of the war, <a href="/wiki/William_D._Rubinstein" class="mw-redirect" title="William D. Rubinstein">William D. Rubinstein</a> wrote: </p>
      <p>"The normal estimate is that of a Paraguayan population of somewhere between 450,000 and 900,000, only 220,000 survived the war, of whom only 28,000 were adult males."<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the pillaging of Asunción in 1869, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Brazilian_Army" title="Imperial Brazilian Army">Imperial Brazilian Army</a> packed up and transported the Paraguayan National Archives to <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> Brazil's records from the war have remained classified.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> This has made Paraguayan history in the Colonial and early National periods difficult to research and study. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chacokrieg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Chacokrieg.jpg/220px-Chacokrieg.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Chacokrieg.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="313"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chacokrieg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a> (1932–35), in which Bolivia lost most of the disputed territory to Paraguay
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg/220px-Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg/330px-Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg/440px-Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg 2x" data-file-width="662" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Paraguayan recruits during the Chaco war
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1904 the Liberal revolution against the rule of Colorados broke out. The Liberal rule started a period of great political instability. Between 1904 and 1954 Paraguay had thirty-one <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">presidents</a>, most of whom were removed from office by force.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> Conflicts between the factions of the ruling Liberal party led to the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_Civil_War_(1922)" title="Paraguayan Civil War (1922)">Paraguayan Civil War of 1922</a>. </p>
      <p>The unresolved border conflict with Bolivia over the Chaco region finally erupted in the early 1930s in the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a>. After great losses Paraguay defeated Bolivia and established its sovereignty over most of the disputed Chaco region. After the war, military officers used popular dissatisfaction with the Liberal politicians to seize the power for themselves. On 17 February 1936, the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution_(Paraguay)" title="February Revolution (Paraguay)">February Revolution</a> brought colonel <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Franco" title="Rafael Franco">Rafael Franco</a> to power. Between 1940 and 1948, the country was ruled by general <a href="/wiki/Higinio_Mor%C3%ADnigo" title="Higinio Morínigo">Higinio Morínigo</a>. Dissatisfaction with his rule resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_Civil_War_(1947)" title="Paraguayan Civil War (1947)">Paraguayan civil war of 1947</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> In its aftermath <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Stroessner" title="Alfredo Stroessner">Alfredo Stroessner</a> began involvement in a string of plots, which resulted in his military <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> of 4 May 1954. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Stroessner_era.2C_1954.E2.80.931989"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stroessner_era,_1954–1989">Stroessner era, 1954–1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stroessner era, 1954–1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/El_Stronato" title="El Stronato">El Stronato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A series of unstable governments ensued until the establishment in 1954 of the regime of dictator <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Stroessner" title="Alfredo Stroessner">Alfredo Stroessner</a>, who remained in office for more than three decades until 1989. Paraguay was modernized to some extent under Stroessner's regime, although his rule was marked by extensive human rights abuses.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Stroessner and the <i>Colorado</i> party ruled the country from 1954 to 1989. The dictator oversaw an era of economic expansion, but also had a poor human rights and environmental record (see "Political History"). Paraguay actively participated in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> Torture and death for political opponents was routine. After his overthrow, the <i>Colorado</i> continued to dominate national politics until 2008. </p>
      <p>The splits in the <i>Colorado</i> Party in the 1980s, and the prevailing conditions – Stroessner's advanced age, the character of the regime, the economic downturn, and <a href="/wiki/International_isolation" title="International isolation">international isolation</a> – were catalysts for anti-regime demonstrations and statements by the opposition prior to the 1988 general elections.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Authentic_Radical_Liberal_Party" title="Authentic Radical Liberal Party">PLRA</a></i> leader <a href="/wiki/Domingo_La%C3%ADno" title="Domingo Laíno">Domingo Laíno</a> served as the focal point of the opposition in the second half of the 1980s. The government's effort to isolate Laíno by exiling him in 1982 had backfired. On his sixth attempt to re-enter the country in 1986, Laíno returned with three television crews from the U.S., a former United States ambassador to Paraguay, and a group of Uruguayan and Argentine congressmen. Despite the international contingent, the police violently barred Laíno's return.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Stroessner regime relented in April 1987, and permitted Laíno to return to Asunción. Laíno took the lead in organizing demonstrations and reducing infighting among the opposition party. The opposition was unable to reach agreement on a common strategy regarding the elections, with some parties advocating abstention, and others calling for blank voting. The parties held numerous 'lightning demonstrations' (<i>mítines relámpagos</i>), especially in rural areas. Such demonstrations were gathered and quickly disbanded before the arrival of the police. </p>
      <p>In response to the upsurge in opposition activities, Stroessner condemned the Accord for advocating "sabotage of the general elections and disrespect of the law". He used national police and civilian <a href="/wiki/Vigilantes" class="mw-redirect" title="Vigilantes">vigilantes</a> of the <i>Colorado</i> Party to break up demonstrations. A number of opposition leaders were imprisoned or otherwise harassed. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hermes_Rafael_Saguier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hermes Rafael Saguier (page does not exist)">Hermes Rafael Saguier</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermes_Rafael_Saguier" class="extiw" title="es:Hermes Rafael Saguier">es</a>]</span>, another key leader of the <i>PLRA</i>, was imprisoned for four months in 1987 on charges of sedition. In early February 1988, police arrested 200 people attending a National Coordinating Committee meeting in <a href="/wiki/Coronel_Oviedo" title="Coronel Oviedo">Coronel Oviedo</a>. Laíno and several other opposition figures were arrested before dawn on the day of the election, 14 February, and held for twelve hours. The government declared Stroessner's re-election with 89% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The opposition attributed the results in part to the virtual Colorado monopoly on the mass media. They noted that 53% of those polled indicated that there was an "uneasiness" in Paraguayan society. 74% believed that the political situation needed changes, including 45% who wanted a substantial or total change. Finally, 31% stated that they planned to abstain from voting in the February elections.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Stroessner.27s_overthrow.2C_post-1989"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stroessner's_overthrow,_post-1989">Stroessner's overthrow, post-1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Stroessner's overthrow, post-1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 3 February 1989, Stroessner was overthrown in a military coup headed by General <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(President)" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrés Rodríguez (President)">Andrés Rodríguez</a>. As president, Rodríguez instituted political, legal, and economic reforms and initiated a <i>rapprochement</i> with the international community. Reflecting the deep hunger of the rural poor for land, hundreds immediately occupied thousands of acres of unused territories belonging to Stroessner and his associates; by mid-1990, 19,000 families occupied 340,000 acres (138,000&nbsp;ha). At the time, 2.06 million people lived in rural areas, more than half of the 4.1 million total population, and most were landless.<sup id="cite_ref-nagel_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nagel-48">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The June 1992 constitution established a democratic system of government and dramatically improved protection of fundamental human rights. In May 1993, Colorado Party candidate <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Wasmosy" title="Juan Carlos Wasmosy">Juan Carlos Wasmosy</a> was elected as Paraguay's first civilian president in almost forty years, in what international observers deemed free and fair elections. </p>
      <p>With support from the United States, the Organization of American States, and other countries in the region, the Paraguayan people rejected an April 1996 attempt by then Army Chief General <a href="/wiki/Lino_Oviedo" title="Lino Oviedo">Lino Oviedo</a> to oust President Wasmosy. </p>
      <p>Oviedo was nominated as the Colorado candidate for president in the 1998 election. However, when the Supreme Court upheld in April his conviction on charges related to the 1996 coup attempt, he was not allowed to run and was detained in jail. His former running mate, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Cubas" class="mw-redirect" title="Raúl Cubas">Raúl Cubas</a>, became the Colorado Party's candidate, and was elected in May in elections deemed by international observers to be free and fair. One of Cubas' first acts after taking office in August was to commute Oviedo's sentence and release him. In December 1998, Paraguay's Supreme Court declared these actions unconstitutional. In this tense atmosphere, the murder of Vice President and long-time Oviedo rival <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mar%C3%ADa_Arga%C3%B1a" title="Luis María Argaña">Luis María Argaña</a> on 23 March 1999, led the Chamber of Deputies to impeach Cubas the next day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 26 March, eight student anti-government demonstrators were murdered, widely believed to have been carried out by Oviedo supporters. This increased opposition to Cubas, who resigned on 28 March. Senate President <a href="/wiki/Luis_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Macchi" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis González Macchi">Luis González Macchi</a>, a Cubas opponent, was peacefully sworn in as president the same day. </p>
      <p>In 2003, Nicanor Duarte Frutos was elected as president. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_of_Fernando_Lugo">Election of Fernando Lugo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Election of Fernando Lugo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>For the 2008 general elections, the Colorado Party was favored in polls. Their candidate was Minister of Education <a href="/wiki/Blanca_Ovelar" title="Blanca Ovelar">Blanca Ovelar</a>, the first woman to be nominated as a candidate for a major party in Paraguayan history. After sixty years of Colorado rule, voters chose <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Lugo" title="Fernando Lugo">Fernando Lugo</a>, a former Roman Catholic Bishop and not a professional politician in civil government, and a member of the Authentic Radical Liberal Party, Paraguay's largest opposition party. Lugo was an adherent of <a href="/wiki/Liberation_theology" title="Liberation theology">liberation theology</a>. Lugo achieved a historic victory in Paraguay's presidential election, defeating the ruling party candidate, and ending 61 years of conservative rule. Lugo won with nearly 41% of the vote, compared to almost 31% for Blanca Ovelar of the Colorado party.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> Outgoing President <a href="/wiki/Nicanor_Duarte" title="Nicanor Duarte">Nicanor Duarte Frutos</a> hailed the moment as the first time in the history of the nation that a government had transferred power to opposition forces in a constitutional and peaceful fashion. </p>
      <p>Lugo was sworn in on 15 August 2008. The Lugo administration set its two major priorities as the reduction of corruption and economic inequality.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-50">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg/220px-Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg/330px-Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg/440px-Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="380"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Inauguration of former President <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Cartes" title="Horacio Cartes">Horacio Cartes</a>, 15 August 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Political instability following Lugo's election and disputes within his cabinet encouraged some renewal of popular support for the Colorado Party. Reports suggested that the businessman Horacio Cartes became the new political figure amid disputes. Despite the US <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a>'s strong accusations against Cartes related to <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">drug trafficking</a>, he continued to amass followers in the political arena. </p>
      <p>On 14 January 2011, the Colorado Party convention nominated Horacio Cartes as the presidential candidate for the party. However, the party's constitution did not allow it.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 21 June 2012, <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Fernando_Lugo" title="Impeachment of Fernando Lugo">impeachment proceedings against President Lugo</a> began in the country's lower house, which was controlled by his opponents. Lugo was given less than twenty-four hours to prepare for the proceedings and only two hours in which to mount a defense.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-51">[49]</a></sup> Impeachment was quickly approved and the resulting trial in Paraguay's Senate, also controlled by the opposition, ended with the removal of Lugo from office and Vice President Federico Franco assuming the duties of president.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN22_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN22-52">[50]</a></sup> Lugo's rivals blamed him for the deaths of 17 people – eight police officers and nine farmers – in armed clashes after police were ambushed by armed peasants when enforcing an eviction order against rural trespassers.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lugo's supporters gathered outside Congress to protest the decision as a "politically motivated coup d'état".<sup id="cite_ref-CNN22_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN22-52">[50]</a></sup> Lugo's removal from office on 22 June 2012 is considered by <a href="/wiki/UNASUR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNASUR">UNASUR</a> and other neighboring countries, especially those currently governed by leftist leaders, as a coup d'état.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> However, the Organization of American States, which sent a mission to Paraguay to gather information, concluded that the impeachment process was not a coup d'état, as it had been carried out in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Paraguay" title="Constitution of Paraguay">Constitution of Paraguay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Present_day">Present day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Present day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>From August 2013 to 15 August 2018, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">President of Paraguay</a> was <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Cartes" title="Horacio Cartes">Horacio Cartes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> Since 15 August 2018, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">President of Paraguay</a> is <a href="/wiki/Mario_Abdo_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Mario Abdo Benítez">Mario Abdo Benítez</a>. They are both from conservative <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Party_(Paraguay)" title="Colorado Party (Paraguay)">Colorado Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Paraguay" title="Geography of Paraguay">Geography of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:194px;max-width:194px">

        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px">

           <a href="/wiki/File:Salto_del_%C3%91acunday_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Salto_del_%C3%91acunday_-_panoramio.jpg/190px-Salto_del_%C3%91acunday_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Salto_del_%C3%91acunday_-_panoramio.jpg/285px-Salto_del_%C3%91acunday_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Salto_del_%C3%91acunday_-_panoramio.jpg/380px-Salto_del_%C3%91acunday_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672"></a>

           <a href="/wiki/Nacunday_National_Park" title="Nacunday National Park">Nacunday National Park</a>, Paraguay

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay is divided by the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Paraguay" class="mw-redirect" title="Río Paraguay">Río Paraguay</a> into two well differentiated geographic regions. The eastern region (Región Oriental); and the western region, officially called Western Paraguay (Región Occidental) and also known as the Chaco, which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a>. The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_south" title="19th parallel south">19°</a> and <a href="/wiki/28th_parallel_south" title="28th parallel south">28°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/54th_meridian_west" title="54th meridian west">54°</a> and <a href="/wiki/63rd_meridian_west" title="63rd meridian west">63°W</a>. </p>
      <p>The terrain consists mostly of grassy plains and wooded hills in the eastern region. To the west are mostly low, marshy plains. Paraguay contains six terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Alto_Paran%C3%A1_Atlantic_forests" title="Alto Paraná Atlantic forests">Alto Paraná Atlantic forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Chaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerrado" title="Cerrado">Cerrado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humid_Chaco" title="Humid Chaco">Humid Chaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantanal" title="Pantanal">Pantanal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_flooded_savanna" title="Paraná flooded savanna">Paraná flooded savanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-58">[56]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.39/10, ranking it 74th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-59">[57]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guarani_Aquifer" title="Guarani Aquifer">Guarani Aquifer</a> is an important <a href="/wiki/Open_and_closed_lakes" title="Open and closed lakes">exorheic basin</a> to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Paraguay" title="Climate of Paraguay">Climate of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1340" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_PRY_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Paraguay map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The overall climate is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a> to <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical</a>. Like most lands in the region, Paraguay has only wet and dry periods. Winds play a major role in influencing Paraguay's weather: between October and March, warm winds blow from the Amazon Basin in the north, while the period between May and August brings cold winds from the Andes. </p>
      <p>The absence of mountain ranges to provide a natural barrier allows winds to develop speeds as high as 161&nbsp;km/h (100&nbsp;mph). This also leads to significant changes in temperature within a short span of time; between April and September, temperatures will sometimes drop below freezing. January is the hottest summer month, with an average daily temperature of 28.9 degrees Celsius (84 degrees F). </p>
      <p>Rainfall varies dramatically across the country, with substantial rainfall in the eastern portions, and semi-arid conditions in the far west. The far eastern forest belt receives an average of 170 centimeters (67 inches) of rain annually, while the western Chaco region typically averages no more than 50&nbsp;cm (20&nbsp;in) a year. The rains in the west tend to be irregular and evaporate quickly, contributing to the aridity of the area. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Paraguay" title="Politics of Paraguay">Politics of Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Paraguay" title="Human rights in Paraguay">Human rights in Paraguay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Paraguay" title="Foreign relations of Paraguay">Foreign relations of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay is a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative democratic">representative democratic</a> republic, with a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a> across three branches. Executive power is exercised solely by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">President</a>, who is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in the two chambers of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Paraguay" title="Congress of Paraguay">National Congress</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial Branch">judiciary</a> is vested on <a href="/wiki/Tribunals" class="mw-redirect" title="Tribunals">tribunals</a> and Courts of <a href="/wiki/Civil_Law_(legal_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil Law (legal system)">Civil Law</a> and a nine-member Supreme Court of Justice, all of them independent of the executive and the legislature. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Paraguay" title="Armed Forces of Paraguay">Armed Forces of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG/220px-Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG/330px-Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG/440px-Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Paraguayan marines at Ancon Marine Base
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Paraguay" title="Armed Forces of Paraguay">military of Paraguay</a> consist of an <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navy</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Naval_aviation" title="Naval aviation">naval aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marines" title="Marines">marine corps</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Air_force" title="Air force">air force</a>. <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Paraguay" title="Constitution of Paraguay">Paraguay's constitution</a> establishes the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">president of Paraguay</a> as <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Paraguay has <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">compulsory military service</a>; all 18-year-old males, as well as 17-year-old males in the year of their 18th birthday, are liable for one year of <a href="/wiki/Active_duty" title="Active duty">active duty</a>. While the constitution allows for <a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objector" title="Conscientious objector">conscientious objection</a>, no enabling legislation has yet been approved. </p>
      <p>Paraguay has partnered with Argentina, Brazil, and the United States in regional anti-terrorism and anti-narcotics efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> In July 2005, U.S. <a href="/wiki/Special_forces" title="Special forces">special forces</a> began arriving at Paraguay's <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Estigarribia" title="Mariscal Estigarribia">Mariscal Estigarribia</a> air base to support joint training and humanitarian operations<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clarin_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clarin-64">[62]</a></sup> In 2019, Asuncion hosted the first meeting of the Regional Security Mechanism (RSM), which promotes cooperation between Paraguay, Argentina, Brazil, and the U.S. in addressing <a href="/wiki/Transnational_crime" title="Transnational crime">transnational crime</a> and terrorism in the "triple frontier" region.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Paraguay ratified the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>, thus banning the development, testing, production, stockpiling, stationing, and transfer of nuclear weapons in its territory, as well as forbidding assistance and encouragement to the prohibited activities.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_Divisions">Administrative Divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administrative Divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Paraguay" title="Departments of Paraguay">Departments of Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Paraguay" title="Districts of Paraguay">Districts of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay consists of seventeen departments and one capital district (<i>distrito capital</i>). </p>
      <p>It is also divided into two regions: The "Occidental Region" or Chaco (Boquerón, Alto Paraguay and Presidente Hayes), and the "Oriental Region" (the other departments and the capital district). </p>
      <p>These are the departments, with their capitals, population, area and the number of districts: </p>
