      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Paraguay" title="Economy of Paraguay">Economy of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 1970 and 2013, the country had the highest economic growth of South America,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> with an average rate of 7.2% per year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2010 and 2013, Paraguay experienced the greatest economic expansion of South America, with a GDP growth rate of 14.5% and 13.6% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2005 the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> explained that less than 10% of workers in Paraguay participate in the <a href="/wiki/Pension" title="Pension">pension</a> system, 95% of which is administered by two institutions. Both are financed on a <a href="/wiki/Pay_as_you_go_pension_plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Pay as you go pension plan">pay as you go</a> system by worker contributions; the first, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Instituto_de_Previsi%C3%B3n_Social&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Instituto de Previsión Social (page does not exist)">Instituto de Previsión Social</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instituto_de_Previsi%C3%B3n_Social_(Paraguay)" class="extiw" title="es:Instituto de Previsión Social (Paraguay)">es</a>]</span> is for private sector employees, and the <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">caja fiscal</i> for public employees (including university professors, teachers, judicial employees, army officers and police officers) and veterans of the Chaco War (or their descendants).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>All of <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Paraguay" title="Electricity sector in Paraguay">Paraguay's electricity</a> is generated by <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydropower</a>, making it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_electricity_production_from_renewable_sources" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by electricity production from renewable sources">cleanest in the world</a>. Paraguay has an installed electrical production capacity of 8,110 MW, producing 63 billion kWh/year in 2016; with domestic consumption of just 15 billion kWh, the excess production is sold to Brazil, Argentina, and Uruguay, making Paraguay the world's largest exporter of electric power.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> This production is from two large <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric power">hydroelectric power</a> projects along its borders, including the <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a>, the world's second largest generating station. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="854" data-file-height="667"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Paraguay's product exports in 28 color-coded categories, 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay is the fifth-largest <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybean</a> producer in the world<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> and second-largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Stevia" title="Stevia">stevia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The market economy is distinguished by a large informal sector, featuring re-export of imported consumer goods to neighboring countries, as well as the activities of thousands of microenterprises and urban street vendors. Nonetheless, over the last 10 years the Paraguayan economy diversified dramatically, with the energy, auto parts and clothing industries leading the way.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country also boasts the third most important free commercial zone in the world: <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_del_Este" title="Ciudad del Este">Ciudad del Este</a>, trailing behind <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> A large percentage of the population, especially in rural areas, derives its living from agricultural activity, often on a subsistence basis. Because of the importance of the informal sector, accurate economic measures are difficult to obtain. The economy grew rapidly between 2003 and 2013 as growing world demand for commodities combined with high prices and favorable weather to support Paraguay's commodity-based export expansion. </p>
      <p>In 2012, Paraguay's government introduced the MERCOSUR (FOCEM) system in order to stimulate the economy and job growth through a partnership with both Brazil and Argentina.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_manufacturing">Industry and manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Industry and manufacturing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BBVA_Paraguay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BBVA_Paraguay.jpg/170px-BBVA_Paraguay.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BBVA_Paraguay.jpg/255px-BBVA_Paraguay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BBVA_Paraguay.jpg/340px-BBVA_Paraguay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1815" data-file-height="2722"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BBVA_Paraguay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Banco_Bilbao_Vizcaya_Argentaria" title="Banco Bilbao Vizcaya Argentaria">BBVA</a> Paraguay
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mineral_industry_of_Paraguay" title="Mineral industry of Paraguay">mineral industry of Paraguay</a> produces about 25% of the country's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) and employs about 31% of the labor force. Production of <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> occurs commonly throughout Paraguay's industrial sector. The growth of the industry was further fueled by the <a href="/wiki/Maquila" class="mw-redirect" title="Maquila">maquila</a> industry, with large industrial complexes located in the eastern part of the country. Paraguay put in place many incentives aimed to attract industries to the country. One of them is the so-called "Maquila law" by which companies can relocate to Paraguay, enjoying minimal tax rates.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical industry</a>, Paraguayan companies now<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> meet 70% of domestic consumption and have begun to export drugs. Paraguay is quickly<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (February 2016)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> supplanting foreign suppliers in meeting the country's drug needs.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> Strong growth also is evident in the production of edible oils, garments, organic sugar, meat processing, and steel.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2003 manufacturing made up 13.6% of the GDP, and the sector employed about 11% of the working population in 2000. Paraguay's primary manufacturing focus is on food and beverages. Wood products, paper products, hides and furs, and non-metallic mineral products also contribute to manufacturing totals. Steady growth in the manufacturing GDP during the 1990s (1.2% annually) laid the foundation for 2002 and 2003, when the annual growth rate rose to 2.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues">Social issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Social issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290">
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2014</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Various poverty estimates suggest that 30–50% of the population is poor.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> In rural areas, 41.20% of the people lack a monthly income to cover basic necessities, whereas in urban centers this figure is 27.6%. The top 10% of the population holds 43.8% of the national income, while the lowest 10% has 0.5%. The economic recession has worsened income inequality, notably in the rural areas, where the <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> has risen from 0.56 in 1995 to 0.66 in 1999. </p>
      <p>More recent data (2009)<sup id="cite_ref-abc.com.py_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc.com.py-81">[79]</a></sup> show that 35% of the Paraguayan population is poor, 19% of which live in extreme poverty. Moreover, 71% of the latter live in rural areas of the country. </p>
      <p>Similarly, land concentration in the Paraguayan countryside is one of the highest in the globe: 10% of the population controls 66% of the land, while 30% of the rural people are landless.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> In the immediate aftermath of the 1989 overthrow of Stroessner, some 19,000 rural families occupied hundreds of thousands of acres of unused lands formerly held by the dictator and his associates by mid-1990, but many rural poor remained landless. This inequality has caused a great deal of tensions between the landless and land owners.<sup id="cite_ref-nagel_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nagel-48">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues_of_the_indigenous">Social issues of the indigenous</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Social issues of the indigenous">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Literacy rates are extremely low among Paraguay's indigenous population, who have a literacy rate of 7.1% compared to the 51% rate of the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-paho_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paho-83">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Only 2.5% of Paraguay's indigenous population has access to clean drinking water and only 9.5% have electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-paho_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paho-83">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

        <div class="thumbcaption">

        </div>

      <p>Paraguay's population is distributed unevenly through the country, with the vast majority of people living in the eastern region near the capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunción">Asunción</a>, which accounts for 10% of the country's population. The <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> region, which includes the <a href="/wiki/Alto_Paraguay_Department" title="Alto Paraguay Department">Alto Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boquer%C3%B3n_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Boquerón Department">Boquerón</a> and <a href="/wiki/Presidente_Hayes_Department" title="Presidente Hayes Department">Presidente Hayes Department</a>, and accounts for about 60% of the territory, is home to less than 2% of the population. About 56% of Paraguayans live in urban areas, making Paraguay one of the least urbanized nations in South America. </p>
      <p>For most of its history, Paraguay has been a recipient of immigrants, owing to its low population density, especially after the demographic collapse caused by the Paraguayan War. Immigrants include Italians, Germans, Russians, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Paraguayan" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Paraguayan">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_Paraguay" title="Koreans in Paraguay">Koreans</a>, Chinese, <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_migration_to_Paraguay" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese migration to Paraguay">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Paraguay" title="Ukrainians in Paraguay">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, Brazilians, and Argentines. Paraguay has one of the most prominent <a href="/wiki/Germans_in_Paraguay" title="Germans in Paraguay">German</a> communities in South America, with some 25,000 German-speaking <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Paraguay" title="Mennonites in Paraguay">Mennonites</a> living in the Paraguayan <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Chaco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> German settlers founded several towns, such as <a href="/wiki/Hohenau,_Paraguay" title="Hohenau, Paraguay">Hohenau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filadelfia" title="Filadelfia">Filadelfia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuland_Colony" title="Neuland Colony">Neuland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obligado" title="Obligado">Obligado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Germania" title="Nueva Germania">Nueva Germania</a>. Several websites that promote German immigration to Paraguay claim that 5–7% of the population is of German ancestry,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (April 2014)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Paraguay#Dubious" title="Talk:Paraguay">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> including 150,000 people of German-Brazilian descent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Citations are from many German immigration promotion websites, there must be more objective sources for this (April 2014)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> Paraguay has also been a haven for communities persecuted for the religious faith, like the <a href="/wiki/Bruderhof_Communities" title="Bruderhof Communities">Bruderhof</a> who were forced to leave England in 1941 because of their pacifist beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> Many of these communities have retained their languages and culture, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian people">Brazilians</a>, who represent the largest and most prominent immigrant group, at around 400,000.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> Many Brazilian Paraguayans are of German, Italian and Polish descent.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> There are an estimated 63,000 <a href="/wiki/Afro-Paraguayans" title="Afro-Paraguayans">Afro-Paraguayans</a>, comprising 1% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (April 2014)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Caacupe5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Caacupe5.jpg/220px-Caacupe5.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Caacupe5.jpg/330px-Caacupe5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/Caacupe5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="266"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Caacupe5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A gathering in <a href="/wiki/Caacup%C3%A9" title="Caacupé">Caacupé</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There is no official data on the ethnic composition of the Paraguayan population, as the Department of Statistics, Surveys and Censuses of Paraguay does not ask about <i>race</i> and <i>ethnicity</i> in census surveys, although it does inquire about the indigenous population.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> According to the census of 2002, indigenous people made up 1.7% of Paraguay's total population.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Traditionally, the majority of the Paraguayan population is considered mixed (<i>mestizo</i> in Spanish). HLA-DRB1 polymorphism studies have shown genetic distances between Paraguayans and Spanish populations were closer than between Paraguayans and Guaranis, suggesting the predominance of Spanish genetics among Paraguayans.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> According to the 2019 revision of the World Population Prospects<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-84">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-85">[83]</a></sup>, Paraguay has a population of 6,956,066, of which 95% are Mestizo or white and 5% are labelled as "other", which includes members of 17 distinct ethnolinguistic indigenous groups, many of which are poorly documented. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg/170px-Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg/255px-Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg/340px-Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Main Catholic Chapel in <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n,_Paraguay" title="Concepción, Paraguay">Concepción, Paraguay</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Paraguay" title="Religion in Paraguay">Religion in Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Christianity, particularly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, is the dominant religion in Paraguay.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> According to the 2002 census, 89.9% of the population was Catholic, 6.2% was <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestant</a>, 1.1% identified with other Christian sects, and 0.6% practiced indigenous religions. A U.S. State Department report on Religious Freedom names Roman Catholicism, evangelical Protestantism, mainline Protestantism, Judaism (Orthodox, Conservative, and Reform), <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a> as prominent religious groups. It also mentions a large Muslim community in <a href="/wiki/Alto_Paran%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Alto Paraná">Alto Paraná</a> (as a result of Middle-Eastern immigration, especially from <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>) and a prominent Mennonite community in Boquerón.<sup id="cite_ref-state1_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state1-101">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Paraguay" title="Languages of Paraguay">Languages of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay is a bilingual nation. Both <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guaraní</a> are official languages. The Guaraní language is a remarkable trace of the indigenous Guaraní culture that has endured in Paraguay. Guaraní claims its place as one of the last surviving and thriving of South American indigenous national languages. In 2015, Spanish was spoken by about 87% of the population, while Guaraní is spoken by more than 90%, or slightly more than 5.8 million speakers. 52% of rural Paraguayans are bilingual in Guaraní. While Guaraní is still widely spoken, Spanish is generally given a preferential treatment in government, business, media and education as one of South America's <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua francas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue-list_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-list-102">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div>
      <p> There are approximately 19 other indigenous languages spoken in Paraguay, many of which are threatened by extinction. Languages such as Guana, Ayoreo and Ishir (Chamacoco) are considered endangered.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Paraguay" title="Culture of Paraguay">Culture of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Paraguay" title="Music of Paraguay">Music of Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Paraguay" title="Cinema of Paraguay">Cinema of Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Paraguay's cultural heritage can be traced to the extensive <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage" title="Interracial marriage">intermarriage</a> between the original male Spanish settlers and indigenous <a href="/wiki/Guarani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Guarani people">Guaraní</a> women. Their culture is highly influenced by various European countries, including Spain. Therefore, Paraguayan culture is a fusion of two cultures and traditions; one European, the other, Southern Guaraní. More than 93% of Paraguayans are <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizos">mestizos</a></i>, making Paraguay one of the most homogeneous countries in Latin America. A characteristic of this cultural fusion is the extensive bilingualism present to this day: more than 80% of Paraguayans speak both <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and the indigenous language, <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Guaraní language">Guaraní</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jopara" title="Jopara">Jopara</a>, a mixture of Guaraní and Spanish, is also widely spoken.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg/220px-Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg/330px-Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg/440px-Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3386" data-file-height="2640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ovecha Ragué Festival
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>This cultural fusion is expressed in arts such as embroidery (<i>ao po'í</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Nanduti" class="mw-redirect" title="Nanduti">lace making</a> (<i>ñandutí</i>). The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Paraguay" title="Music of Paraguay">music of Paraguay</a>, which consists of lilting polkas, bouncy <i>galopas,</i> and languid <i><a href="/wiki/Guarania_(music)" title="Guarania (music)">guaranias</a></i> is played on the native harp. Paraguay's culinary heritage is also deeply influenced by this cultural fusion. Several popular dishes contain <a href="/wiki/Manioc" class="mw-redirect" title="Manioc">manioc</a>, a local staple crop similar to the <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">yuca</a> also known as Cassava root found in the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwestern United States</a> and Mexico, as well as other indigenous ingredients. A popular dish is <i><a href="/wiki/Sopa_paraguaya" title="Sopa paraguaya">sopa paraguaya</a></i>, similar to a thick <a href="/wiki/Corn_bread" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn bread">corn bread</a>. Another notable food is <i><a href="/wiki/Chipa" title="Chipa">chipa</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Bagel" title="Bagel">bagel</a>-like bread made from <a href="/wiki/Cornmeal" title="Cornmeal">cornmeal</a>, manioc, and cheese. Many other dishes consist of different kinds of cheeses, onions, bell peppers, cottage cheese, cornmeal, milk, seasonings, butter, eggs and fresh corn kernels. </p>
      <p>The 1950s and 1960s were the time of the birth of a new generation of Paraguayan novelists and poets such as <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ricardo_Maz%C3%B3" title="José Ricardo Mazó">José Ricardo Mazó</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_Vallejos" title="Roque Vallejos">Roque Vallejos</a>, and Nobel Prize nominee <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Roa_Bastos" title="Augusto Roa Bastos">Augusto Roa Bastos</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Paraguay" title="Cinema of Paraguay">Paraguayan films</a> have been made. </p>
      <p>Inside the family, conservative values predominate. In lower classes, <a href="/wiki/Godparent" title="Godparent">godparents</a> have a special relationship to the family, since usually, they are chosen because of their favorable social position, in order to provide extra security for the children. Particular respect is owed them, in return for which the family can expect protection and patronage.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Paraguay" title="Sport in Paraguay">Sport in Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg/220px-Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg/330px-Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg/440px-Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco_en_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Defensores_del_Chaco" title="Estadio Defensores del Chaco">Estadio Defensores del Chaco</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunción">Asunción</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sport in Paraguay is an important part of the country's national culture. <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport, and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> is also very popular.<sup id="cite_ref-Paraguay_in_Pictures_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paraguay_in_Pictures-109">[107]</a></sup> Other sports such as <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> are also popular.<sup id="cite_ref-Paraguay_in_Pictures_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paraguay_in_Pictures-109">[107]</a></sup> Additional Paraguayan sports and pastimes include <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">motorsport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Paraguay" title="Education in Paraguay">Education in Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Paraguay" title="List of universities in Paraguay">List of universities in Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_Paraguay" class="mw-redirect" title="List of high schools in Paraguay">List of high schools in Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">Literacy</a> was about 93.6% and 87.7% of Paraguayans finish the 5th grade according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s last Educational Development Index 2008. Literacy does not differ much by gender.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-110">[108]</a></sup> A more recent study<sup id="cite_ref-abc.com.py_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc.com.py-81">[79]</a></sup> reveals that attendance at primary school by children between 6 and 12 years old is about 98%. Primary education is free and mandatory and takes nine years. Secondary education takes three years.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-110">[108]</a></sup> Main universities in Paraguay include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Asunci%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="National University of Asunción">National University of Asunción</a> (public and founded in 1889)<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Autonomous_University_of_Asunci%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous University of Asunción">Autonomous University of Asunción</a> (private and founded in 1979)<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Universidad_Cat%C3%B3lica_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Asunci%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Católica Nuestra Señora de la Asunción">Universidad Católica Nuestra Señora de la Asunción</a> (private and run by the church).<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Universidad_Americana" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Americana">Universidad Americana</a> (private).</li> 
       <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Universidad_del_Pac%C3%ADfico_(Paraguay)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Universidad del Pacífico (Paraguay) (page does not exist)">Universidad del Pacífico</a> (private and founded in 1991).</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The net primary enrollment rate was at 88% in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_110-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-110">[108]</a></sup> Public expenditure on education was about 4.3% of GDP in the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_110-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-110">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Paraguay" title="Health in Paraguay">Health in Paraguay</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Average life expectancy in Paraguay is rather high given its poverty: as of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it was 75 years,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> equivalent to far wealthier Argentina, and the 8th highest in the Americas according to World Health Organization. Public expenditure on health is 2.6% of GDP, while private health expenditure is 5.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_110-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-110">[108]</a></sup> Infant mortality was 20 per 1,000 births in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_110-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-110">[108]</a></sup> Maternal mortality was 150 per 100,000 live births in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_110-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-110">[108]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> has helped the Paraguayan government reduce the country's maternal and infant mortality. The <i>Mother and Child Basic Health Insurance Project</i> aimed to contribute to reducing mortality by increasing the use of selected life-saving services included in the country's Mother and Child Basic Health Insurance Program (MCBI) by women of child-bearing age, and children under age six in selected areas. To this end, the project also targeted improving the quality and efficiency of the health service network within certain areas, in addition to increasing the Ministry of Public Health and Social Welfare's (MSPBS) management.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734">
      <div class="reflist">

         <li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFStearns" class="citation book cs1">Stearns, Peter N.          <li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193339-40-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193339-40_27-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFCunninghame_Graham1933">Cunninghame Graham 1933</a>, p.&nbsp;39-40.<span class="error harv-error" style="display: none; font-size:100%"> sfn error: no target: CITEREFCunninghame_Graham1933 (<a href="/wiki/Category:Harv_and_Sfn_template_errors" title="Category:Harv and Sfn template errors">help</a>)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193341-42-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193341-42_28-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFCunninghame_Graham1933">Cunninghame Graham 1933</a>, p.&nbsp;41-42.<span class="error harv-error" style="display: none; font-size:100%"> sfn error: no target: CITEREFCunninghame_Graham1933 (<a href="/wiki/Category:Harv_and_Sfn_template_errors" title="Category:Harv and Sfn template errors">help</a>)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Robert Cowley, <i>The Reader's Encyclopedia to Military History</i>. New York, New York: Houston Mifflin, 1996. Page 479.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Hooker-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Hooker_30-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hooker, T.D., 2008, The Paraguayan War, Nottingham: Foundry Books, 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1901543153" title="Special:BookSources/1901543153">1901543153</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Robert Phillimore (1860), <i>A Statement of the Facts of the Controversy Between the Governments of Great Britain and Paraguay</i>, page 2. William Moore Printing. Washington D.C. USA.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson186910-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson186910_32-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFThompson1869">Thompson 1869</a>, p.&nbsp;10.<span class="error harv-error" style="display: none; font-size:100%"> sfn error: no target: CITEREFThompson1869 (<a href="/wiki/Category:Harv_and_Sfn_template_errors" title="Category:Harv and Sfn template errors">help</a>)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Blanco Party of Uruguay, hardline right wing and reactionary at those days, was in the Uruguayan Government during the outbreak of the war and were allies of the Paraguayan Government. See the classic book of the Blanco Leader Luis Alberto de Herrera (1927): "El Drama del 65 – La Culpa Mitrista", pp. 11 – 33. Bareiro y Ramos Editors. Montevideo, Uruguay</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sir Richard Francis Burton: "Letters from the Battlefields of Paraguay", p.76 – Tinsley Brothers Editors – London (1870) – Burton, as a witness of the conflict, marks this date (12–16 October 1864) as the real beginning of the war. He writes (and it's the most logic account, considering the facts): <i>The Brazilian Army invades the Banda Oriental, despite the protestations of President López, who declared that such invasion would be held a "casus belli"</i>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pomer, León (2008): "La Guerra del Paraguay: Estado, Política y Negocios" (in Spanish), pp. 240 – 241. Buenos Aires: Editorial Colihue.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hooker, T.D., 2008, "The Paraguayan War". Nottingham: Foundry Books, pp. 105–108. 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1901543153" title="Special:BookSources/1901543153">1901543153</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The classical view asserts that Francisco Solano López's expansionist and hegemonic views are the main reason for the outbreak of the conflict. The traditional Paraguayan view, held by the "<i>lopistas</i>" (supporters of Solano López, both in Paraguay and worldwide), affirms that Paraguay acted in self-defense and for the protection of the "Equilibrium of the Plate Basin". This view is usually contested by the "<i>anti-lopistas</i>" (also known in Paraguay as "<i>legionarios</i>"), who favoured the "Triple Alliance". Revisionist views, both from right and left wing national-populists, put a great emphasis on the influence of the British Empire in the conflict, a view that is discarded by a majority of historians.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFRubinsein2004" class="citation book cs1">Rubinsein, W. D.          <li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hipólito Sanchez Quell: "Los 50.000 Documentos Paraguayos Llevados al Brasil". Ediciones Comuneros, Asunción (2006).</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some of the documents taken by Brasil during the war, were returned to Paraguay in the collection known as "Colección de Río Branco", nowadays in the National Archives of Asunción, Paraguay</span> </li>
